	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en"><i>American Idol</i> (season 7)</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="summary" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-style: italic; background: #CCCCFF; padding: 0.25em 1em; line-height: 1.5em;"><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:American_Idol_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="American Idol logo.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3c/American_Idol_logo.png/250px-American_Idol_logo.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="157" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/3c/American_Idol_logo.png 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="188" /></a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="summary" style="text-align:center;background: #CCCCFF; padding: 0.25em 1em; line-height: 1.5em;">Season 7</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Broadcast from</th><td>January 15&#160;–<br />May 21, 2008</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Judges</th><td><a href="/wiki/Paula_Abdul" title="Paula Abdul">Paula Abdul</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">Simon Cowell</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Randy_Jackson" title="Randy Jackson">Randy Jackson</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Host(s)</th><td><a href="/wiki/Ryan_Seacrest" title="Ryan Seacrest">Ryan Seacrest</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Broadcaster</th><td><a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox Broadcasting Company</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Finals venue</th><td class="location"><a href="/wiki/Nokia_Theatre_L.A._Live" class="mw-redirect" title="Nokia Theatre L.A. </th></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="summary" style="text-align:center;background: #CCCCFF; padding: 0.25em 1em; line-height: 1.5em;">Runner-up</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/David_Archuleta" title="David Archuleta">David Archuleta</a></td></tr><tr class="noprint"><th colspan="2" class="summary" style="text-align:center;background: #CCCCFF; padding: 0.25em 1em; line-height: 1.5em;">Chronology</th></tr><tr class="noprint hlist" style="font-weight: bold;"><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_6)" title="American Idol (season 6)">◀</a></li>
<li>2008</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_8)" title="American Idol (season 8)">▶</a></li></ul>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The seventh season of <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i>, the annual reality show and singing competition, began on January 15, 2008, and concluded on May 21, 2008. <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Seacrest" title="Ryan Seacrest">Ryan Seacrest</a> continued to host the show with <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">Simon Cowell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paula_Abdul" title="Paula Abdul">Paula Abdul</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Randy_Jackson" title="Randy Jackson">Randy Jackson</a> returning as judges. <a href="/wiki/David_Cook_(singer)" title="David Cook (singer)">David Cook</a> was announced the winner of the competition on May 21, 2008, defeating runner-up <a href="/wiki/David_Archuleta" title="David Archuleta">David Archuleta</a> by a margin of roughly 12 million votes out of over 97 million, which was at that time the highest recorded vote total in the show's history. The split was 56 to 44%.
</p><p>The seventh season was the first season during which neither the winner nor the runner-up was ever in the bottom group during any week before the finale on May 21, 2008. It was also the second season during which both the winner and the runner-up were male contestants, with the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_2)" title="American Idol (season 2)">second season</a> being the first.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Changes_from_past_seasons">Changes from past seasons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Changes from past seasons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Prior to the start of the seventh season, Executive Producer <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Lythgoe" title="Nigel Lythgoe">Nigel Lythgoe</a> admitted that the sixth season had placed more focus on the guest mentors than the contestants.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Changes were planned for the seventh season designed to return attention to the contestants by providing more information on their backgrounds and families.
</p><p>A major change for the seventh season was allowing contestants to play musical instruments,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-newyorkpost_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorkpost-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> an element that originated on <i><a href="/wiki/Australian_Idol" title="Australian Idol">Australian Idol</a></i> and can also be seen on Norway's <i><a href="/wiki/Idol_(Norway)" class="mw-redirect" title="Idol (Norway)">Idol</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Canadian_Idol" title="Canadian Idol">Canadian Idol</a></i>.  A brand new set was built, and a new introduction credit sequence was created. The season finale also moved from the <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Theatre" title="Dolby Theatre">Kodak Theatre</a> to the larger <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Theater" title="Microsoft Theater">Nokia Theatre</a> in Los Angeles, which would be the venue for the live series finale for the next six years.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_auditions">Regional auditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Regional auditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<th colspan="6">Total Tickets to Hollywood
</th>
<th>164
</th></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Contestants were required to be between the ages of 16 and 28 on July 28, 2007, and eligible to work in the United States. Those ineligible include former contestants who had previously reached the semifinal of the first through third seasons, or the last phase of Hollywood round of fourth through sixth seasons (top 44 of the fourth and fifth seasons, top 40 of the sixth season), those holding recording or management contracts, or those who were not US citizens or landed immigrants (i.e. permanent residents).
</p><p>One auditioner this year, <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Cohen" title="Alexis Cohen">Alexis Cohen</a>, gained media attention due to her outraged reaction and profuse profanities after the judges rejected her in the Philadelphia audition.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>  She also returned in season eight to audition in New York and her audition was featured.  She was later found dead in a hit-and-run accident.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another auditioner who gained some public attention was <a href="/wiki/Renaldo_Lapuz" title="Renaldo Lapuz">Renaldo Lapuz</a>, who sang his own composition "We're Brothers Forever", which he wrote for Simon Cowell.  He was later asked to return to perform in the finale.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hollywood_week">Hollywood week</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Hollywood week">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Hollywood week took place at the <a href="/wiki/Pasadena_Civic_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Pasadena Civic Center">Pasadena Civic Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena, California</a>, over a period of five days. A total of 164 contestants were invited from the seven audition cities. This year, the process was altered slightly to ensure that no talent would be prematurely dismissed.  The contestants were allowed two performances before elimination, and the group round was removed.
</p><p>The first round of individual performances lasted two days.  For the first time ever, contestants had the option of either being accompanied by the band or playing an instrument themselves. Some were shown playing the keyboard, guitar, or even the drums. If the judges approved of the contestantss performances, they received a "free pass" to the third and final round of performances, and 48 contestants were given this "free pass".  Unlike previous seasons, contestants whose performances not considered good enough were given a second chance in the second round. They lined up on stage in groups of 10 and each sang a short segment of a song <i><a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a></i>. After each group had finished, the judges cut those they felt not talented enough.  Almost 100 were eliminated in this round.
</p><p>In the final round, all the remaining contestants performed individually a song chosen from a large list of songs provided, accompanied by the band and three backup singers.  After each performance, the judges decided whether or not to cut the contestant. By the end of the day, only 50 contestants remained. The judges then deliberated further on who should be in the top 24, and their decision was revealed the next day in the" Green Mile" episode.
</p><p>One of the more prominent contestants during the Hollywood week was <a href="/wiki/Josiah_Leming" title="Josiah Leming">Josiah Leming</a>, whose unhappiness with the backing band resulted in him dismissing the band.  He was cut in the "Green Mile" episode.  Another piece of drama involved contestant Kyle Ensley when Simon Cowell voiced strong objection over him not being selected for the semifinals.  His nonselection was later revealed to have resulted in serious rift between Simon Cowell and the show producer Nigel Lythgoe.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Semifinalists">Semifinalists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Semifinalists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22American+Idol%22+season+7">"American Idol"&#160;season 7</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22American+Idol%22+season+7+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22American+Idol%22+season+7+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22American+Idol%22+season+7+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22American+Idol%22+season+7">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22American+Idol%22+season+7&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Adore_Delano" title="Adore Delano">Daniel 'Danny' Noriega</a> (born September 29, 1989 in <a href="/wiki/Azusa,_California" title="Azusa, California">Azusa, California</a>, 18 at the time of the show) auditioned in San Diego. He previously auditioned for <i>Idol</i> in the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_6)" title="American Idol (season 6)">sixth season</a> and made it to Hollywood week, but was cut in the first round. His elimination song was Soft Cell's version of "Tainted Love". Shortly following his elimination, Noriega received an offer from Rosie O'Donnell to perform on her cruise.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Luke Menard (29 at the time of the show) auditioned in <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha</a> with "<a href="/wiki/Bend_and_Break" title="Bend and Break">Bend and Break</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Keane_(band)" title="Keane (band)">Keane</a>. In Hollywood, he sang "<a href="/wiki/Arthur%27s_Theme_(Best_That_You_Can_Do)" title="Arthur&#39;s Theme (Best That You Can Do)">Arthur's Theme (Best That You Can Do)</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Cross" title="Christopher Cross">Christopher Cross</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Grace_Kelly_(song)" title="Grace Kelly (song)">Grace Kelly</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Mika_(singer)" title="Mika (singer)">Mika</a>. He auditioned for the sixth season in <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Tennessee" title="Memphis, Tennessee">Memphis</a> and sang "<a href="/wiki/How_Deep_Is_Your_Love_(Bee_Gees_song)" title="How Deep Is Your Love (Bee Gees song)">How Deep Is Your Love</a>", but did not make it to Hollywood. Prior to the seventh season of <i>Idol</i>, he was a member of the <i><a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a></i> group <a href="/wiki/Chapter_6_(band)" title="Chapter 6 (band)">Chapter 6</a>.</li>
<li>Robert "Robbie" Carrico (26 at the time of the show) is from <a href="/wiki/Melbourne,_Florida" title="Melbourne, Florida">Melbourne, Florida</a>, and auditioned for the show in Miami. His professional singing career prior to <i>American Idol</i> includes being a member of the pop group <a href="/wiki/Boyz_N_Girlz_United" title="Boyz N Girlz United">Boyz N Girlz United</a>, which opened for <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> during her "<a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_Tour" title="...Baby One More Time Tour">...Baby One More Time Tour</a>" in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-mtv_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtv-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Columbus_Dispatch_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Columbus_Dispatch-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Jason Yeager<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> (28 at the time of the show) is from <a href="/wiki/Grand_Prairie,_Texas" title="Grand Prairie, Texas">Grand Prairie, Texas</a>, and auditioned in Dallas. He appeared and was a finalist on the first season of <i><a href="/wiki/Making_the_Band" title="Making the Band">Making the Band</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> reality show that led to the formation of boy band <a href="/wiki/O-Town" title="O-Town">O-Town</a>.</li>
<li>Colton Berry (18 at the time of the show) is from <a href="/wiki/Staunton,_Virginia" title="Staunton, Virginia">Staunton, Virginia</a>. He auditioned in Charleston.</li>
<li>Garrett Haley (17 at the time of the show) is from <a href="/wiki/Elida,_Ohio" title="Elida, Ohio">Elida, Ohio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> He auditioned in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>.</li>
<li>Asia'h Epperson (19 at the time of the show) is from <a href="/wiki/Joplin,_Missouri" title="Joplin, Missouri">Joplin, Missouri</a>, and auditioned in Atlanta singing "<a href="/wiki/How_Do_I_Live" title="How Do I Live">How Do I Live</a>." Two days before the auditions, her father died in a car accident. Her elimination song was "I Wanna Dance With Somebody" by Whitney Houston.</li>
<li>Kady Malloy (18 at the time of the show) is from <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, Texas, and auditioned in Dallas. She became known on the show for her impersonation of <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> and can also impersonate several other artists. Malloy is trained in <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a> singing. Her elimination song was "<a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants to Live Forever">Who Wants to Live Forever</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>. She has released several songs to her MySpace and shot a video for a cover of "<a href="/wiki/Time_After_Time_(Cyndi_Lauper_song)" title="Time After Time (Cyndi Lauper song)">Time After Time</a>" with Colton Berry. Simon's comment after her audition was: "Out of all of the people we have seen during this season you are the best."</li>
<li>Alaina Whitaker (17 at the time of the show) is from <a href="/wiki/Tulsa,_Oklahoma" title="Tulsa, Oklahoma">Tulsa, Oklahoma</a>, and auditioned in Dallas. She was a member of the female country group Della Rose along with Andrea Young and Erin James. Before the show, her sister and she won a talent competition in Tulsa. Her group Della Rose was working on their debut album in Nashville before they disbanded. The group has opened up for several major country acts including <a href="/wiki/Travis_Tritt" title="Travis Tritt">Travis Tritt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Keith_Anderson" title="Keith Anderson">Keith Anderson</a>, who was also known as the group's mentor.</li>
<li>Alexandréa Lushington (17 at the time of the show) is from <a href="/wiki/Douglasville,_Georgia" title="Douglasville, Georgia">Douglasville, Georgia</a>, and auditioned in Atlanta. In 2004, she sang against fellow <i>Idol</i> semifinalist David Archuleta on an episode of the television show <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Search" title="Star Search">Star Search</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Columbus_Dispatch_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Columbus_Dispatch-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joanne_Borgella" title="Joanne Borgella">Joanne Borgella</a> (25 at the time of the show) was a model from <a href="/wiki/Hoboken,_New_Jersey" title="Hoboken, New Jersey">Hoboken, New Jersey</a>, who auditioned in Philadelphia. Before auditioning for <i>Idol</i>, she appeared in and won <i><a href="/wiki/Mo%27Nique%27s_Fat_Chance" title="Mo&#39;Nique&#39;s Fat Chance">Mo'Nique's Fat Chance</a></i>.</li>
<li>Amy Davis (25 at the time of the show) is professional model from <a href="/wiki/Lowell,_Indiana" title="Lowell, Indiana">Lowell, Indiana</a>, who auditioned in Dallas.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Semifinals">Semifinals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Semifinals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Finalists">Finalists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Finalists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22American+Idol%22+season+7">"American Idol"&#160;season 7</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22American+Idol%22+season+7+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22American+Idol%22+season+7+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22American+Idol%22+season+7+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22American+Idol%22+season+7">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22American+Idol%22+season+7&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="4" style="margin:0 1em 1em 0; text-align:left;">

<tbody><tr>
<td valign="top"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DavidCookNOLA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/DavidCookNOLA.jpg/100px-DavidCookNOLA.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/DavidCookNOLA.jpg/150px-DavidCookNOLA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/DavidCookNOLA.jpg/200px-DavidCookNOLA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DavidCookNOLA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>David Cook</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/David_Cook_(singer)" title="David Cook (singer)">David Cook</a> (born December 20, 1982 in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, 24 at the time of the auditions and 25 at the time of the show) is a native of <a href="/wiki/Blue_Springs,_Missouri" title="Blue Springs, Missouri">Blue Springs, Missouri</a>, who auditioned in Omaha with <a href="/wiki/Bon_Jovi" title="Bon Jovi">Bon Jovi</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Livin%27_On_A_Prayer" class="mw-redirect" title="Livin&#39; On A Prayer">Livin' On A Prayer</a>". Cook's interest in music began early in life; he received his first guitar at the age of 2.<sup id="cite_ref-wordnerd_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wordnerd-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>  He formed a band while still at high school called <a href="/wiki/Axium" title="Axium">Axium</a>, which was chosen as the best band in Kansas City in 2004. He later joined <a href="/wiki/Midwest_Kings" title="Midwest Kings">Midwest Kings</a> in Tulsa, but left to pursue a solo project where he released an album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Analog_Heart" title="Analog Heart">Analog Heart</a></i>.  Prior to <i>Idol</i>, he worked as a <a href="/wiki/Bartender" title="Bartender">bartender</a> at the "Blank Slate" in Tulsa, where he  also occasionally played shows.  He enjoys doing crossword puzzles in his spare time and calls himself a "word nerd".<sup id="cite_ref-wordnerd_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wordnerd-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>  His Hollywood performance of <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Adams" title="Bryan Adams">Bryan Adams</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/(Everything_I_Do)_I_Do_It_for_You" title="(Everything I Do) I Do It for You">(Everything I Do) I Do It for You</a>" did not impress Simon Cowell, but did so with his second performance, <a href="/wiki/Edwin_McCain" title="Edwin McCain">Edwin McCain</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/I%27ll_Be_(Edwin_McCain_song)" title="I&#39;ll Be (Edwin McCain song)">I'll Be</a>".  He wore an orange wristband to support a seven-year-old fan with leukemia from top-12 week onward. He was never in the "bottom three".  On May 21, 2008, he was declared the winner.  He was signed to <a href="/wiki/RCA_Records" title="RCA Records">RCA Records</a> and released a <a href="/wiki/David_Cook_(album)" title="David Cook (album)">self-titled</a> album on November 18, 2008.
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td valign="top"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Archuleta_in_parade.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/David_Archuleta_in_parade.jpg/100px-David_Archuleta_in_parade.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/David_Archuleta_in_parade.jpg/150px-David_Archuleta_in_parade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/David_Archuleta_in_parade.jpg/200px-David_Archuleta_in_parade.jpg 2x" data-file-width="982" data-file-height="1399" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Archuleta_in_parade.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>David Archuleta</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/David_Archuleta" title="David Archuleta">David Archuleta</a> (born December 28, 1990 in <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, 16 at the time of the auditions and 17 at the time of the show) is from <a href="/wiki/Murray,_Utah" title="Murray, Utah">Murray, Utah</a>, who auditioned in San Diego with <a href="/wiki/John_Mayer" title="John Mayer">John Mayer</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Waiting_on_the_World_to_Change" title="Waiting on the World to Change">Waiting on the World to Change</a>". In 2003, at the age of 12, he sang on several episodes of the television show <i>Star Search</i><sup id="cite_ref-Columbus_Dispatch_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Columbus_Dispatch-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and went on to win the season finale and the $100,000 grand prize.<sup id="cite_ref-CBS_Star_Search_Official_site_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBS_Star_Search_Official_site-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>  In one episode, he competed against Alexandréa Lushington, who was a fellow semifinalist this season. He suffered from vocal paralysis after that show, which affected one of his vocal cords.  He impressed the judges with his performance of <a href="/wiki/Gnarls_Barkley" title="Gnarls Barkley">Gnarls Barkley</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Crazy_(Gnarls_Barkley_song)" title="Crazy (Gnarls Barkley song)">Crazy</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Adams" title="Bryan Adams">Bryan Adams</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Heaven_(Bryan_Adams_song)" title="Heaven (Bryan Adams song)">Heaven</a>" during the Hollywood round.  He was never in the "bottom three" and finished as the season-seven runner-up. He was signed to <a href="/wiki/Jive_Records" title="Jive Records">Jive Records</a>.
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Syesha_Mercado.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Syesha_Mercado.jpg/100px-Syesha_Mercado.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Syesha_Mercado.jpg/150px-Syesha_Mercado.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Syesha_Mercado.jpg/200px-Syesha_Mercado.jpg 2x" data-file-width="787" data-file-height="974" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Syesha_Mercado.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Syesha Mercado</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Syesha_Mercado" title="Syesha Mercado">Syesha Mercado</a> (born January 2, 1987 in <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport,_Connecticut" title="Bridgeport, Connecticut">Bridgeport, Connecticut</a>, 21 at the time of the show) is from <a href="/wiki/Sarasota,_Florida" title="Sarasota, Florida">Sarasota, Florida</a>, who auditioned in Miami with <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">Aretha Franklin</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Think_(Aretha_Franklin_song)" title="Think (Aretha Franklin song)">Think</a>". She is a student at <a href="/wiki/Florida_International_University" title="Florida International University">Florida International University</a> and has been singing and dancing since she was a child. During Hollywood week, she became ill and almost completely lost her voice. In preparation for her final Hollywood performance with Aretha Franklin's "<a href="/wiki/Chain_of_Fools_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chain of Fools (song)">Chain of Fools</a>", she went on voice rest and wrote down everything she had to say on a pad of paper.  Prior to <i>American Idol</i>, she appeared on the short-lived US version of <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Academy" title="Star Academy">Star Academy</a></i> (known as <i><a href="/wiki/The_One:_Making_a_Music_Star" title="The One: Making a Music Star">The One: Making a Music Star</a></i> when it aired on ABC in July 2006 for two weeks).  <a href="/wiki/Kara_DioGuardi" title="Kara DioGuardi">Kara DioGuardi</a>, who was one of the coaches on the Endemol franchise, joined <i>Idol</i> for season eight.<sup id="cite_ref-Herald_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herald-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>  She was voted off as a third-place finisher.
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td valign="top"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JasonCastro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/JasonCastro.jpg/100px-JasonCastro.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/JasonCastro.jpg/150px-JasonCastro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/JasonCastro.jpg/200px-JasonCastro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="924" data-file-height="1334" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JasonCastro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jason Castro</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jason_Castro_(singer)" title="Jason Castro (singer)">Jason Castro</a> (born March 25, 1987, 20 at the time of the show) from <a href="/wiki/Rockwall,_Texas" title="Rockwall, Texas">Rockwall, Texas</a> auditioned in Dallas with <a href="/wiki/Keith_Urban" title="Keith Urban">Keith Urban</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Once_in_a_Lifetime_(Keith_Urban_song)" title="Once in a Lifetime (Keith Urban song)">"Once in a Lifetime"</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ray_LaMontagne" title="Ray LaMontagne">Ray LaMontagne</a>'s version of Gnarls Barkley's  "Crazy". He started in music playing the drums. In high school, he played for a band, Keeping Lions, which has since disbanded.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>  In 2006, he appeared on <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_Kimball" title="Cheyenne Kimball">Cheyenne Kimball</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Reality_television" title="Reality television">reality TV series</a>, as her real-life dating interest. Castro is the first person in his family, which is originally from <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, to be born in the United States. He is a student at <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University" title="Texas A&amp;M University">Texas A&amp;M University</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Construction_science" class="mw-redirect" title="Construction science">construction science</a> major and music minor. He began growing his hair out for <a href="/wiki/Dreadlocks" title="Dreadlocks">dreadlocks</a> during his senior year of high school.  He exited the competition in fourth place.
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td valign="top"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooke_White.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Brooke_White.jpg/100px-Brooke_White.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Brooke_White.jpg/150px-Brooke_White.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Brooke_White.jpg/200px-Brooke_White.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1029" data-file-height="1319" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooke_White.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Brooke White</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brooke_White" title="Brooke White">Brooke White</a> (born June 2, 1983 in <a href="/wiki/Mesa,_Arizona" title="Mesa, Arizona">Mesa, Arizona</a>, 24 at time of the show) was a nanny from <a href="/wiki/Van_Nuys,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Van Nuys, California">Van Nuys, California</a>; she  auditioned in Philadelphia with <a href="/wiki/Corinne_Bailey_Rae" title="Corinne Bailey Rae">Corinne Bailey Rae</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Like_a_Star" title="Like a Star">Like a Star</a>". During her audition, she admitted to never having seen an <a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_Association_of_America_film_rating_system" title="Motion Picture Association of America film rating system">R-rated</a> movie, prompting Cowell to state that the show will "bring her over to the dark side." In 2005, she released an album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Songs_from_the_Attic" title="Songs from the Attic">Songs from the Attic</a></i> under New Millennium Records.  She performed <a href="/wiki/Carole_King" title="Carole King">Carole King</a>'s "Beautiful" on Hollywood week.  She finished in fifth place.  After the contest, she started her own record label, June Baby Records, with Randy Jackson, and released an album, <i><a href="/wiki/High_Hopes_%26_Heartbreak" title="High Hopes &amp; Heartbreak">High Hopes &amp; Heartbreak</a></i>.
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carly_Smithson_in_parade.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Carly_Smithson_in_parade.jpg/100px-Carly_Smithson_in_parade.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Carly_Smithson_in_parade.jpg/150px-Carly_Smithson_in_parade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Carly_Smithson_in_parade.jpg/200px-Carly_Smithson_in_parade.jpg 2x" data-file-width="966" data-file-height="1260" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carly_Smithson_in_parade.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Carly Smithson</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Carly_Smithson" title="Carly Smithson">Carly Smithson</a> (born as Carly Hennessy on September 12, 1983, in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, Ireland, 24 at the time of the show) is a professional singer and <a href="/wiki/Bartender" title="Bartender">bartender</a>/<a href="/wiki/Waitress" class="mw-redirect" title="Waitress">waitress</a> from <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>, where she has been living for the past three years. Smithson previously signed a recording contract with major US label <a href="/wiki/MCA_Records" title="MCA Records">MCA Records</a> and released an album in 2001 entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Ultimate_High" title="Ultimate High">Ultimate High</a></i> under her birth name, Carly Hennessy. The album sold about 300 copies in the first three months following its release. Smithson was originally auditioned in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas</a> during the fifth season, but was dropped from the show due to a problem with her <a href="/wiki/Visa_(document)" class="mw-redirect" title="Visa (document)">visa</a>.  She auditioned in San Diego with <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Every_Woman" title="I&#39;m Every Woman">I'm Every Woman</a>", and performed <a href="/wiki/Leo_Sayer" title="Leo Sayer">Leo Sayer</a>'s version of "<a href="/wiki/When_I_Need_You" title="When I Need You">When I Need You</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Heart_(band)" title="Heart (band)">Heart</a>'s version of  "<a href="/wiki/Alone_(Heart_song)" title="Alone (Heart song)">Alone</a>" in the Hollywood rounds. She finished sixth in the show.
</p>
</td></tr>

<td valign="top"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kristy_Lee_Cook.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Kristy_Lee_Cook.jpg/100px-Kristy_Lee_Cook.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Kristy_Lee_Cook.jpg/150px-Kristy_Lee_Cook.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Kristy_Lee_Cook.jpg/200px-Kristy_Lee_Cook.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1955" data-file-height="2460" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kristy_Lee_Cook.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kristy Lee Cook</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kristy_Lee_Cook" title="Kristy Lee Cook">Kristy Lee Cook</a> (born January 18, 1984, 24 at the time of the show) is a horse trainer from <a href="/wiki/Selma,_Oregon" title="Selma, Oregon">Selma, Oregon</a>.  She sold her prized horse  to afford the trip to audition in Philadelphia, where she auditioned with "<a href="/wiki/Amazing_Grace" title="Amazing Grace">Amazing Grace</a>", a song she also performed during the Hollywood week. In 2001, she was signed to a major label, <a href="/wiki/Arista_Nashville" title="Arista Nashville">Arista Nashville</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Columbus_Dispatch_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Columbus_Dispatch-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bmi_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmi-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Cook also signed with Britney Spears' production company, and Spears herself was supposed to have a cameo in Cook's first video.<sup id="cite_ref-Columbus_Dispatch_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Columbus_Dispatch-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bmi_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmi-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> At the time of signing, she was managed by the former manager of <a href="/wiki/LeAnn_Rimes" title="LeAnn Rimes">LeAnn Rimes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Columbus_Dispatch_25-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Columbus_Dispatch-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bmi_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmi-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<td valign="top"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Michael_Johns_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Michael_Johns_2.jpg/100px-Michael_Johns_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Michael_Johns_2.jpg/150px-Michael_Johns_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Michael_Johns_2.jpg/200px-Michael_Johns_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1276" data-file-height="1567" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Michael_Johns_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Michael Johns</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Michael_Johns_(singer)" title="Michael Johns (singer)">Michael Johns</a> (October 20, 1978 – August 1, 2014, born as Michael Lee in <a href="/wiki/Perth,_Western_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Perth, Western Australia">Perth, Western Australia</a>, aged 29 at the time of the show) auditioned in San Diego with <a href="/wiki/Otis_Redding" title="Otis Redding">Otis Redding</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/I%27ve_Been_Loving_You_Too_Long" title="I&#39;ve Been Loving You Too Long">I've Been Loving You Too Long</a>". He moved to the U.S. from Australia in 1998 and lived in <a href="/wiki/Buckhead,_Atlanta" class="mw-redirect" title="Buckhead, Atlanta">Buckhead, Atlanta</a> for six years, performing at local venues solo and with local band Film. Afterwards, he lived in Los Angeles. After recording a demo and traveling to Los Angeles to showcase for a number of labels in 2001, he signed with <a href="/wiki/Maverick_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Maverick Records">Maverick Records</a> and formed a rock band called The Rising.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Before focusing on his singing career, he was a sportsman, winning a tennis scholarship<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> and playing <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Australian rules football</a> for the <a href="/wiki/USAFL" class="mw-redirect" title="USAFL">USAFL</a> club Atlanta Kookaburras.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> During the Hollywood round, he performed <a href="/wiki/The_Doors" title="The Doors">The Doors</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Light_My_Fire" title="Light My Fire">Light My Fire</a>" but it was his performance of <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen's</a> <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a> that was one of the highlights of that week.  He was eliminated on April 10 and finished in eighth place. Johns died on August 1, 2014, making him the first <i>American Idol</i> finalist to die.<sup id="cite_ref-Patrick_Gomez_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Patrick_Gomez-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</td></tr>

<td valign="top"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RamieleMalubay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/RamieleMalubay.jpg/100px-RamieleMalubay.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/RamieleMalubay.jpg/150px-RamieleMalubay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/RamieleMalubay.jpg/200px-RamieleMalubay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="902" data-file-height="1054" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RamieleMalubay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ramiele Malubay</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ramiele_Malubay" title="Ramiele Malubay">Ramiele Malubay</a> (born September 6, 1987 in Saudi Arabia,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> 20 at the time of that show) <a href="/wiki/Filipino_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Filipino people">Filipino</a>-American from <a href="/wiki/Miramar,_Florida" title="Miramar, Florida">Miramar, Florida</a>, auditioned in Miami with Aretha Franklin's <a href="/wiki/(You_Make_Me_Feel_Like)_A_Natural_Woman" title="(You Make Me Feel Like) A Natural Woman">"Natural Woman"</a>. Prior to auditioning on <i>Idol</i>, she was a nursing student at <a href="/wiki/Broward_Community_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Broward Community College">Broward Community College</a> and worked part-time at a <a href="/wiki/Sushi" title="Sushi">sushi</a> restaurant. She started Polynesian dancing when she was in the first grade and started singing at the age of 12. Since the age of 12, Ramiele has sung at various Filipino-American events.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>  She performed Aretha Franklin's "<a href="/wiki/Until_You_Come_Back_to_Me_(That%27s_What_I%27m_Gonna_Do)" title="Until You Come Back to Me (That&#39;s What I&#39;m Gonna Do)">Until You Come Back to Me</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Kiki_Dee" title="Kiki Dee">The Kiki Dee Band</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/I%27ve_Got_The_Music_In_Me" class="mw-redirect" title="I&#39;ve Got The Music In Me">I've Got The Music In Me</a>" at the Hollywood rounds.  She was eliminated in ninth place.
</p>

<td valign="top"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ChikezieEze.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/ChikezieEze.jpg/100px-ChikezieEze.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/ChikezieEze.jpg/150px-ChikezieEze.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/ChikezieEze.jpg/200px-ChikezieEze.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1249" data-file-height="1440" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ChikezieEze.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chikezie</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chikezie" title="Chikezie">Chikezie</a> (born Chikezie Eze on September 11, 1985 in <a href="/wiki/Inglewood,_California" title="Inglewood, California">Inglewood, California</a>, 22 at the time of that show) is a <a href="/wiki/Nigerian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Nigerian American">Nigerian American</a> from <a href="/wiki/Inglewood,_California" title="Inglewood, California">Inglewood, California</a>, who auditioned in San Diego with <a href="/wiki/Luther_Vandross" title="Luther Vandross">Luther Vandross</a>'s version of "<a href="/wiki/All_the_Man_That_I_Need" title="All the Man That I Need">All the Woman I Need</a>".  During the competition, he dropped using his last name because it was so frequently mispronounced ('eh-zee' and not 'EE-zee').<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> He previously auditioned for the show's <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_6)" title="American Idol (season 6)">sixth season</a>, and made it into the Hollywood round, where he was cut before the top 44. Before auditioning for <i>Idol,</i> he worked as a <a href="/wiki/Transportation_Security_Administration" title="Transportation Security Administration">Transportation Security Administration</a> officer at <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles International Airport</a>.
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td valign="top"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AmandaOvermyer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/AmandaOvermyer.jpg/100px-AmandaOvermyer.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/AmandaOvermyer.jpg/150px-AmandaOvermyer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/AmandaOvermyer.jpg/200px-AmandaOvermyer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1070" data-file-height="1515" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AmandaOvermyer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Amanda Overmyer</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Amanda_Overmyer" title="Amanda Overmyer">Amanda Overmyer</a> (born October 26, 1984, 23 at the time of that show) is a <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson" title="Harley-Davidson">Harley</a>-riding nurse is from <a href="/wiki/Mulberry,_Indiana" title="Mulberry, Indiana">Mulberry, Indiana</a>, who auditioned in Atlanta with <a href="/wiki/Janis_Joplin" title="Janis Joplin">Janis Joplin</a>'s "Turtle Blues" and <a href="/wiki/Creedence_Clearwater_Revival" title="Creedence Clearwater Revival">Creedence Clearwater Revival</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Travelin%27_Band" title="Travelin&#39; Band">Travelin' Band</a>". She received a nursing degree from <a href="/wiki/Ivy_Tech_Community_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivy Tech Community College">Ivy Tech Community College</a> and deals predominantly in respiratory issues. She has been the lead singer of several local hard rock bands, including Steeleto and Ruinaces. A week before the Hollywood week, she was injured in a serious car accident.  She performed <a href="/wiki/The_Doors" title="The Doors">The Doors</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Light_My_Fire" title="Light My Fire">Light My Fire</a>" at the Hollywood rounds.  After the season ended, she married her fiancé Casey Taylor.
</p>
</td></tr>

<td valign="top"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DavidHernandez.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/DavidHernandez.jpg/100px-DavidHernandez.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/DavidHernandez.jpg/150px-DavidHernandez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/DavidHernandez.jpg/200px-DavidHernandez.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="1640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DavidHernandez.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>David Hernandez</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/David_Hernandez_(singer)" title="David Hernandez (singer)">David Hernandez</a> (born May 31, 1983 in <a href="/wiki/Glendale,_Arizona" title="Glendale, Arizona">Glendale, Arizona</a>, 24 at the time of that show) is from <a href="/wiki/Glendale,_Arizona" title="Glendale, Arizona">Glendale, Arizona</a>, and auditioned with <a href="/wiki/The_Temptations" title="The Temptations">The Temptations</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Ain%27t_Too_Proud_to_Beg" title="Ain&#39;t Too Proud to Beg">Ain't Too Proud to Beg</a>".  He was a student at <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University" title="Arizona State University">Arizona State University</a> with a major in <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_journalism" title="Broadcast journalism">broadcast journalism</a>. He gave up his apartment to move to <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a>. Until September 30, 2007, Hernandez worked as a male stripper named "Caden" at Dick's Cabaret in <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>, performing fully nude and giving <a href="/wiki/Lap_dance" title="Lap dance">lap dances</a> to male patrons.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> This did not prevent him from being on the show.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>  He performed <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Stills" title="Stephen Stills">Stephen Stills</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Love_the_One_You%27re_With" title="Love the One You&#39;re With">Love the One You're With</a>" on Hollywood week.  He was voted off in 12th place.
</p>

<p><small><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1"><b><a href="#ref_1">^Note 1</a></b></span>  Due to the <i><a href="/wiki/Idol_Gives_Back" title="Idol Gives Back">Idol Gives Back</a></i> special airing on the show's regular Wednesday results night, which was April 9. The results show was moved to Thursday, April 10.</small>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Results_night_performances">Results night performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Results night performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During the Hollywood weeks, "<a href="/wiki/Hollywood%27s_Not_America" title="Hollywood&#39;s Not America">Hollywood's Not America</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Ferras" title="Ferras">Ferras</a> played when contestants were eliminated, while "Best Days" by <a href="/wiki/Graham_Colton" title="Graham Colton">Graham Colton</a> was the elimination song for the semi-finals round. For the finals, <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_2)" title="American Idol (season 2)">season 2</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Ruben_Studdard" title="Ruben Studdard">Ruben Studdard</a> remade <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Loggins" title="Kenny Loggins">Kenny Loggins</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Celebrate_Me_Home_(song)" title="Celebrate Me Home (song)">Celebrate Me Home</a>" as the exit song.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_song">Group song</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Group song">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The contestants also performed medleys of songs from that week's theme.
</p>
<ul><li>Top 24: A medley of songs from the 1960s, including "<a href="/wiki/Needles_and_Pins_(1963_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Needles and Pins (1963 song)">Needles and Pins</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/When_You_Walk_in_the_Room" title="When You Walk in the Room">When You Walk in the Room</a>" by <a href="/wiki/The_Searchers_(band)" title="The Searchers (band)">The Searchers</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Spanish_Harlem_(song)" title="Spanish Harlem (song)">Spanish Harlem</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Ben_E._King" title="Ben E. King">Ben E. King</a>, and "<a href="/wiki/Bend_Me,_Shape_Me" title="Bend Me, Shape Me">Bend Me, Shape Me</a>" by <a href="/wiki/The_American_Breed" title="The American Breed">The American Breed</a>.</li>
<li>Top 20: A medley of songs from the 1970s, including "<a href="/wiki/I_Saw_the_Light_(Todd_Rundgren_song)" title="I Saw the Light (Todd Rundgren song)">I Saw the Light</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Todd_Rundgren" title="Todd Rundgren">Todd Rundgren</a>, "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_a_Heartache" title="It&#39;s a Heartache">It's a Heartache</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Tyler" title="Bonnie Tyler">Bonnie Tyler</a>, "<a href="/wiki/The_Things_We_Do_for_Love_(song)" title="The Things We Do for Love (song)">The Things We Do for Love</a>" by <a href="/wiki/10cc" title="10cc">10cc</a>, and "<a href="/wiki/I_Feel_the_Earth_Move" title="I Feel the Earth Move">I Feel the Earth Move</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Carole_King" title="Carole King">Carole King</a>.</li>
<li>Top 12: A medley of songs by The Beatles including "<a href="/wiki/All_My_Loving" title="All My Loving">All My Loving</a>," "<a href="/wiki/I_Feel_Fine" title="I Feel Fine">I Feel Fine</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Buy_Me_Love" title="Can&#39;t Buy Me Love">Can't Buy Me Love</a>," and "<a href="/wiki/Help!_(song)" title="Help! (song)">Help!</a>."</li>
<li>Top 11: A second medley of Beatles songs including "<a href="/wiki/While_My_Guitar_Gently_Weeps" title="While My Guitar Gently Weeps">While My Guitar Gently Weeps</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Here,_There_and_Everywhere" title="Here, There and Everywhere">Here, There and Everywhere</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Because_(The_Beatles_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Because (The Beatles song)">Because</a>," and "<a href="/wiki/The_End_(The_Beatles_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="The End (The Beatles song)">The End</a>."</li>
<li>Top 10: "<a href="/wiki/Right_Back_Where_We_Started_From" title="Right Back Where We Started From">Right Back Where We Started From</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Maxine_Nightingale" title="Maxine Nightingale">Maxine Nightingale</a>.</li>
<li>Top 9: "<a href="/wiki/9_to_5_(Dolly_Parton_song)" title="9 to 5 (Dolly Parton song)">9 to 5</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Dolly_Parton" title="Dolly Parton">Dolly Parton</a>.</li>
<li>Top 8: "<a href="/wiki/Shout_to_the_Lord" title="Shout to the Lord">Shout to the Lord</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Hillsong_Church" title="Hillsong Church">Hillsong</a>.</li>
<li>Top 7: "<a href="/wiki/One_Sweet_Day" title="One Sweet Day">One Sweet Day</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a> with <a href="/wiki/Boyz_II_Men" title="Boyz II Men">Boyz II Men</a>.</li>
<li>Top 6: "<a href="/wiki/All_I_Ask_of_You" title="All I Ask of You">All I Ask of You</a>" from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera_(1986_musical)" title="The Phantom of the Opera (1986 musical)">The Phantom of the Opera</a></i>.</li>
<li>Top 5: A medley of songs by <a href="/wiki/Neil_Diamond" title="Neil Diamond">Neil Diamond</a>, including "<a href="/wiki/Cracklin%27_Rosie" title="Cracklin&#39; Rosie">Cracklin' Rosie</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Song_Sung_Blue" title="Song Sung Blue">Song Sung Blue</a>," and "<a href="/wiki/Brother_Love%27s_Travelling_Salvation_Show_(song)" title="Brother Love&#39;s Travelling Salvation Show (song)">Brother Love's Travelling Salvation Show</a>."</li>
<li>Top 4: "<a href="/wiki/Reelin%27_in_the_Years" class="mw-redirect" title="Reelin&#39; in the Years">Reelin' in the Years</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Steely_Dan" title="Steely Dan">Steely Dan</a>.</li>
<li>Top 3: "<a href="/wiki/Ain%27t_No_Stoppin%27_Us_Now" title="Ain&#39;t No Stoppin&#39; Us Now">Ain't No Stoppin' Us Now</a>" by <a href="/wiki/McFadden_%26_Whitehead" title="McFadden &amp; Whitehead">McFadden &amp; Whitehead</a>.</li></ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_performances">Other performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Other performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Guest artists may perform songs to promote their work or the show itself, or for charitable purpose. Most performed on the result shows, except for Ruben Studdard at the end of the Top 2 performance show and those on the Idol Gives Back special.  Included is a list of those songs with the impact of performance on the <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">Hot 100</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hot_Digital_Songs" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot Digital Songs">Hot Digital Songs</a> chart for the week.  See <a href="/wiki/Idol_Gives_Back" title="Idol Gives Back">Idol Gives Back</a> for the list of performances in that special episode.

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Idol_Gives_Back">Idol Gives Back</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Idol Gives Back">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Idol_Gives_Back" title="Idol Gives Back">Idol Gives Back</a></div>
<p>The "<a href="/wiki/Idol_Gives_Back" title="Idol Gives Back">Idol Gives Back</a>" initiative returned on April 9 for a second year, with a special start time of 7:30&#160;p.m. ET, running for 150&#160;minutes. Again, proceeds will go to children's charities in Africa and the United States. Unlike "Idol Gives Back 2007" when no finalist was eliminated (and two were eliminated in the following week), Michael Johns was eliminated during "Idol Gives Back 2008."
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>Season 7 contestant Carly Smithson stirred up controversy due to a prior major label record deal she had with MCA Records. It has been reported<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> that MCA spent over 2 million dollars promoting Smithson's previous album "Ultimate High," which she made under the name Carly Hennessy. The album only sold 378 copies but is now available on iTunes. To further complicate things, Randy Jackson worked for MCA during the same period of time that Smithson was signed. The media noted that several of the other season 7 semi-finalists had previously also had record deals, including <a href="/wiki/Kristy_Lee_Cook" title="Kristy Lee Cook">Kristy Lee Cook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brooke_White" title="Brooke White">Brooke White</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Johns_(singer)" title="Michael Johns (singer)">Michael Johns</a> (David Cook released an <a href="/wiki/Analog_Heart" title="Analog Heart">independent solo album</a> and had finished recording a follow-up prior to his audition for the show, but he was never involved with a record label or contract).  According to a poll conducted by AOL Television, 63 percent of those polled believed that contestants who have already had record deals should not be contestants on <i>American Idol</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>  However, Idol rules state that contestants are eligible as long as they are no longer under contract when Idol begins, irrespective of any past contracts.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Hernandez_(singer)" title="David Hernandez (singer)">David Hernandez</a> was revealed by <a href="/wiki/Vote_for_the_Worst" title="Vote for the Worst">VotefortheWorst.com</a> to have worked as a <a href="/wiki/Striptease" title="Striptease">stripper</a> in Phoenix, AZ. According to the owner of Dick's Cabaret, David's job included a routine featuring full nudity and performing lap dances for male clientele.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On the show of April 29, the five remaining contestants each sang two songs. Diverting from their usual format, due to time constraints, the judges' critiques after each performance were instead to be bundled until after both songs were performed. However, after the first round had finished, host <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Seacrest" title="Ryan Seacrest">Ryan Seacrest</a> asked for comments, and judge <a href="/wiki/Paula_Abdul" title="Paula Abdul">Paula Abdul</a>, in discussing <a href="/wiki/Jason_Castro_(singer)" title="Jason Castro (singer)">Jason Castro</a>, delivered feedback on his second song before he had performed it. This has led to speculation that the show is scripted or rigged.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The next day, Abdul claimed on Seacrest's radio show that she listened to the performance in rehearsal and in the rushed atmosphere of the show was confused and thought she was supposed to critique both.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<ul><li>The presence of David Archuleta's father was a matter of some discussion and he was banned from providing his son with musical input during his song preparation.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Releases">Releases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Releases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="iTunes">iTunes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: iTunes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During Season 7, <i>American Idol</i> partnered with <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> to make available for sale exclusive performance videos, live performance singles of the semi-finalists and full-length studio recordings of the songs that contestants performed on the show. In order to keep the competition fair, these singles were not allowed to appear on iTunes sales charts until after the finale.  The contestants' performances during the season were removed from sale soon after the finale.
</p><p>The winning song, "<a href="/wiki/The_Time_of_My_Life_(David_Cook_song)" title="The Time of My Life (David Cook song)">The Time of My Life</a>", was recorded by David Cook and released on May 22, 2008. The song was certified platinum by the RIAA on December 12, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-DC_RIAA_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DC_RIAA-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> It was the first winner's song not to be performed during the competition as the Top 2 each selected a different song from a list of 10 entries in song-writing competition to perform instead. Cook performed "The Time of My Life" after Ryan Seacrest announced him as the winner of Season 7.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Idol">Post-Idol</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Post-Idol">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>David Cook's <a href="/wiki/David_Cook_(album)" title="David Cook (album)">debut album</a> was released on November 18, 2008, on 19 Recordings / RCA Records and was certified platinum by the RIAA on January 22, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-DC_RIAA_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DC_RIAA-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Cook teamed with <a href="/wiki/Grammy" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy">Grammy</a> winning producer Rob Cavallo (<a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kid_Rock" title="Kid Rock">Kid Rock</a>) on the album. A single from the album, "<a href="/wiki/Light_On" title="Light On">Light On</a>", was released and peaked at 20 on the billboard top 100 list.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> His sophomore album, <i>This Loud Morning</i>, was released on June 28, 2011.
</p><p>David Archuleta signed with <a href="/wiki/Jive_Records" title="Jive Records">Jive Records</a> and his <a href="/wiki/David_Archuleta_(album)" title="David Archuleta (album)">self-titled debut album</a> was released on November 11, 2008 and debuted at number two. Archuleta's album certified gold. Archuleta's first single, "<a href="/wiki/Crush_(David_Archuleta_song)" title="Crush (David Archuleta song)">Crush</a>", debuted at number two on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> and number one on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Digital_Songs" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot Digital Songs">Hot Digital Songs</a> chart, giving it the highest single debut of 2008 and the highest single debut in 18 months. The song has sold 1.9 million copies as of January 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._Nielsen_ratings">U.S. Nielsen ratings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: U.S. Nielsen ratings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Season 7 of <i>American Idol</i> overall was the most watched primetime program in the United States for the fourth consecutive year, during the conclusion of the 2007–2008 television season.  The Tuesday episode viewership averaged 27.665 million while the Wednesday episode averaged 26.843 million, taking the top 2 spots for the season.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>  The show helped Fox become the most watched overall television network in the U.S. for the first time in its history (as well as a record first for a non-<a href="/wiki/Big_three_television_networks" class="mw-redirect" title="Big three television networks">Big Three</a> major network in <a href="/wiki/Television_in_the_United_States" title="Television in the United States">American television history</a>), and lead the 18–49 demographic ratings with still-standing largest ever margin since the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_ratings" title="Nielsen ratings">people meter technology</a> in the Nielsen nationwide television tallies during the <a href="/wiki/1985-86_United_States_network_television_schedule" class="mw-redirect" title="1985-86 United States network television schedule">1985–1986 television season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span id="Contestants_who_appeared_in_other_talent_shows.2Fseasons"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Contestants_who_appeared_in_other_talent_shows/seasons">Contestants who appeared in other talent shows/seasons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Contestants who appeared in other talent shows/seasons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul><li>Mishavonna Henson, auditioned in the seventh season and got cut during the Hollywood rounds, returned for the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_8)" title="American Idol (season 8)">eighth season</a> and made it in the top 36.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chikezie" title="Chikezie">Chikezie</a> previously auditioned in the sixth season, but was cut during Hollywood Week.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carly_Smithson" title="Carly Smithson">Carly Smithson</a> previously auditioned in the fifth season under her maiden name "Hennessy", but was cut during Hollywood Week when the paperwork for her work visa failed to come through.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Luke_Menard" class="mw-redirect" title="Luke Menard">Luke Menard</a> previously auditioned in the sixth season, but was denied a golden ticket.</li>
<li>Chris Watson, who originally auditioned in Philadelphia, but was cut in Hollywood Week, returned for the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_12)" title="American Idol (season 12)">twelfth season</a> and made it in the top 40.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Julie_Dubela" title="Julie Dubela">Julie Dubela</a>, who originally auditioned in Miami, but did not advance past through the Hollywood Round, competed in <i><a href="/wiki/American_Juniors" title="American Juniors">American Juniors</a></i> and eliminated in the semi-final stage.</li>
<li>Colton Swon, who originally auditioned in Dallas, but he was cut in the last day of Hollywood Week, competed in the <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._season_4)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Voice (U.S. season 4)">fourth season</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Voice (U.S. TV series)">The Voice</a></i> with his older brother Zach as <a href="/wiki/The_Swon_Brothers" title="The Swon Brothers">The Swon Brothers</a>. They finished third.</li>
<li>Danny Noriega would later compete on the <a href="/wiki/RuPaul%27s_Drag_Race_(season_6)" title="RuPaul&#39;s Drag Race (season 6)">sixth season</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/RuPaul%27s_Drag_Race" title="RuPaul&#39;s Drag Race">RuPaul's Drag Race</a></i> as <a href="/wiki/Adore_Delano" title="Adore Delano">Adore Delano</a> in 2014 where he was runner-up. In 2016, Danny returned for the <a href="/wiki/RuPaul%27s_Drag_Race_All_Stars_(season_2)" title="RuPaul&#39;s Drag Race All Stars (season 2)">second season</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/RuPaul%27s_Drag_Race_All_Stars" title="RuPaul&#39;s Drag Race All Stars">RuPaul's Drag Race All Stars</a></i> where he quit the competition in the second episode placing him ninth overall.</li>
<li>David Archuleta competed on the 2003 revival of <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Search" title="Star Search">Star Search</a>,</i> winning the $100,000 prize in the "Junior Singer" category.</li>
<li>Alexandrea Lushington appeared on the 2003 revival of <a href="/wiki/Star_Search" title="Star Search">Star Search</a>, where she was eliminated by fellow Idol contestant <a href="/wiki/David_Archuleta" title="David Archuleta">David Archuleta</a>.</li>
<li>Jason Yeager previously appeared on the original version of <a href="/wiki/Making_the_Band" title="Making the Band">Making the Band</a>, finishing in the top 25.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joanne_Borgella" title="Joanne Borgella">Joanne Borgella</a> was the winner of the first season of <i><a href="/wiki/Mo%27Nique%27s_Fat_Chance" title="Mo&#39;Nique&#39;s Fat Chance">Mo'Nique's Fat Chance</a>.</i></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Deaths">Deaths</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol_(season_7)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Deaths">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Michael Johns</b>
</p><p>Finalist Michael Johns died in <a href="/wiki/Tustin,_California" title="Tustin, California">Tustin, California</a> on August 1, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-people_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-people-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Orange_County_Coroner_Press_Releases_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Orange_County_Coroner_Press_Releases-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> On November 18, 2014, the coroner reported that Johns had died of <a href="/wiki/Dilated_cardiomyopathy" title="Dilated cardiomyopathy">dilated cardiomyopathy</a>, which inhibited the flow of blood to his body and also caused his heart to enlarge.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Fatty_liver" class="mw-redirect" title="Fatty liver">fatty liver</a> also contributed to his death.<sup id="cite_ref-Patrick_Gomez_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Patrick_Gomez-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Joanne Borgella</b>
</p><p>In October 2013, Semi-Finalist Joanne Borgella posted a video stating she had been diagnosed with cancer.<sup id="cite_ref-Death_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Death-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> She said she was suffering from severe headaches and, upon going to the emergency room to determine the cause of those headaches, discovered that cancer had spread to her brain. Borgella died early on October 18, 2014, at age 32.<sup id="cite_ref-ABCNews_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABCNews-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
